The Language of Grearian

Natively known as: Grear /ɡɹɪə/

...and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind...
ens yi yi eeksed choiths kendged ens lungs flule yi beed rupearmor brurds
Pronunciation: /ɛns jiː jiː iːkst ʧɔɪðz kɛnʤd ɛns lʌŋz fluːl jiː biːd ˈɹuːpɪəmɔː bɹɜːdz/
Grearian word order: and he his hat holding stood and the wind to his wet face turned

Phonological changes (in order of application):

  • l → s / _k
  • K → ʔ / _s
  • s → h / V_V
  • d → r / V_V

Grammar

Main word order: Subject (Prepositional phrase) Object Verb. "Mary opened the door with a key" turns into Mary with a key the door opened.
Adjective order: Adjectives are positioned before the noun.
Adposition: postpositions

Nouns

Nouns have two cases:

  • Ergative is the doer of a verb, when the verb is done to something: dog bites man.
  • Absolutive is used in two scenarios: the doer of a verb when not done to something (dog bites), and the done-to of a verb (man bites dog).
Ergative Suffix -aɪ
cliksai /ˈklɪksaɪ/
doɡ (doinɡ the verb to somethinɡ)
Absolutive No affix
cliks /klɪks/
doɡ (doinɡ the verb, but not to somethinɡ)


Singular No affix
cliks /klɪks/
doɡ
Plural Suffix -ɑ
cliksa /ˈklɪksɑ/
doɡs

Verbs

Present If ends with vowel: Suffix -st
Else: Suffix -ɛst
idzesed /ˈɪdzɛst/
learn
Past No affix
ids /ɪdz/
learned
Remote past Suffix -oʊ
idzo /ˈɪdzoʊ/
learned (lonɡ aɡo)
Future If ends with vowel: Suffix -bz
Else: Suffix -ɛbz
idzebs /ˈɪdzɛbz/
will learn



Imperfective aspect

The ‘imperfective’ aspect refers to ongoing actions, such as I am learning and habitual actions, such as I learn (something new every day).

Grearian uses a standalone particle word for imperfective:

Imperfective Particle before the verb: tɪə -
tear ids /tɪə ɪdz/
learns/is learninɡ


Numbers

Grearian has a base-10 number system:

1 - sprou
2 - brou
3 - ek
4 - squoi
5 - ho
6 - frunch
7 - whur
8 - quilth
9 - woulwased
10 - steicked
11 - steicked ens sprou “ten and one”
100 - peth “hundred”
101 - peth sprou “hundred one”
200 - brou peth
1000 - plush “thousand”

Derivational morphology

Adjective → adverb = Suffix -ɪə
Adjective → noun (the quality of being [adj]) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -θs
Else: Suffix -ɔɪθs
Adjective → verb (to make something [adj]) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -d
Else: Suffix -iːd
Noun → adjective (having the quality of [noun]) = Suffix -iː
Noun → adjective relating to noun (e.g. economy → economic) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -ʧ
Else: Suffix -ɛʧ
Noun to verb = If ends with vowel: Suffix -spt
Else: Suffix -oʊspt
Verb → adjective (result of doing [verb]) = Suffix -æɹst
Tending to = Suffix -ɔː
Verb → noun (the act of [verb]) = Suffix -ɔː
Verb → noun that verb produces (e.g. know → knowledge) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -ŋ
Else: Suffix -ɑŋ
One who [verb]s (e.g. paint → painter) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -st
Else: Suffix -ɛst
Place of (e.g. wine → winery) = Suffix -ɪə
Diminutive = If ends with vowel: Suffix -ɹd
Else: Suffix -ɑɹd
Augmentative = Suffix -ɑ
